Local News 2

200,000 Shanghai Residents Go to Sanbei to Watch the Fair

High Platforms and Pavilions Are Renowned Far and Wide

Costing 2 Million Yuan

The Sanbei High Platforms and Pavilions Fair has not been held for 29 years. This year, the village is preparing for three days of competition, costing 1 million yuan. Today is the first day. Including yesterday, at least 200,000 men and women from Shanghai have gone to Ningbo to watch the fair. Even from Wuhan and other places, a large number of tourists have gone to watch. The situation is recorded as follows:

Ship Crowds

This Sanbei High Platforms and Pavilions Fair is the third time it has been held after the competition. There are fifteen platforms and pavilions, each 36 feet high, carried by 120 people, performing various dramas, and there are also stilts, flesh-body lanterns, etc. Since the preparation, it has been rumored far and wide. In the last ten days, Shanghai residents who have gone to watch, the Shanghai-Ningbo passenger ships Xinjing Tian, Xin Beijing, Xin Ning Shao, Hongxing, and Ningxing have been fully loaded every day. There is no room for latecomers. Including yesterday, more than 200,000 people have gone to Ningbo and transferred to Sanbei to watch the fair. Even from Wuhan, a large number of tourists have taken the Yangtze River ship to Shanghai and then transferred to the Ningbo ship to Sanbei to watch the fair.

Inland River Blockage

According to Ningbo ship crew members, since

the 3rd of this month, the river channel of the Cibei inland river has been blocked by civilian boats and rafts. Within this fair period, it will take at least two weeks to restore traffic. The freight transport in various places has also been suspended. The sedan chairs from Yejiashan to Dongbutou have been fully hired. The Sanbei houses have been raised to ten yuan per room for three days. The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway has also increased trains to transport viewers.

Telegraph to Shanghai to Welcome Du

Shen Yushan, the head of the Sanbei

family who is organizing the High Platforms and Pavilions Fair, telegraphed Yu Qiaqing, Du Yuesheng, and others in Shanghai yesterday, saying that the fair is well-organized, and he fears that there are rumors from afar, so he hopes not to believe them lightly. You are respected by the villagers, and they sincerely ask you to come and stop, and your viewing is very important. Therefore, I especially send a telegram for you to come, and please indicate the itinerary so that I can respectfully welcome you. Shen Yushan.

Huge Spending

When the High Platforms and Pavilions are on the move, the area occupied is very large, so the houses are demolished and the road is paved in advance before it can be held. The three-day fair costs millions of yuan, and the various travel expenses of people from all over the world are also more than one million yuan. The Zhejiang Provincial Government has specially dispatched two companies of soldiers to Cixi to suppress the area through which the fair passes. Lu Siyi, director of the Cixi Public Security Bureau, also led the entire police force and the self-defense regiment to Sanbei to protect it.

Silk Fabric Identification Is Actively Underway

Buyers of Silk Can Check the Certificate at the End of Every Four Bolts

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, in view of the recent mixed quality of silk fabrics and the difficulty in distinguishing them, in order to promote pure silk fabrics made in China, save merchants' ethics, and facilitate the recognition of the public, began to identify silk fabrics on the 11th of this month. Silk factories such as Jinyun have already requested identification, totaling more than a thousand bolts. Miao Zhongxiu, director of the Silk Inspection Department of the bureau, and Guo Limao, a technician, and other technicians went to the Dachang Refining Factory to stamp the silk fabrics to be identified with a certificate stamp at one end of the silk fabrics. In the future, if buyers of silk fabrics want to purchase pure silk fabrics made in China, they can check the certificate at the end of each bolt to identify them, so as not to be fooled. The bureau also received a letter from the Meiyi Dyeing and Finishing Factory yesterday, stating that the factory refines about 30,000 bolts of silk every month and requesting the bureau to send personnel to the factory to identify silk fabrics. The letter has been approved and handed over to the Silk Inspection Department for consideration.

The Silk Industry Will Hold a Meeting to Discuss Relief for Foreign Trade

Vietnamese Guests Talk About the Situation of Chinese Silk Being Hit Hard

The National News Agency reports that Chinese silk has been hit hard by increased tariffs in various countries and competition from Japanese silk in recent years, and foreign trade has been completely stagnant. A reporter interviewed two Vietnamese overseas Chinese who recently returned to China and learned about the situation of Chinese silk in Vietnam, as follows:

Alarming Increase in Customs Duties

A representative said that before the Sino-French New Treaty was signed in the 19th year of the Republic of China, silk, tea, porcelain and other goods transported from our country enjoyed a special tariff because they did not have a significant conflict with French goods. At that time, Chinese goods in Vietnam could be sold smoothly. After the initial signing of the New Treaty, overseas Chinese deeply felt that the transportation of Chinese goods to Vietnam would be greatly affected. Although they had repeatedly telegraphed to our Ministry of Foreign Affairs to pay attention to the content of the New Treaty, our government soon announced its implementation, while the French side did not make any announcement and has not yet approved it, which has been delayed for two years and five months. According to the New Treaty, it is stipulated that the term is five years and it may need to be revised. During these two years and five months, overseas Chinese in Vietnam are treated like citizens of countries without treaties. Chinese goods entering Vietnam are also subject to the collection of tariffs as countries without treaties, from special tariffs (i.e., the lowest tariffs) to equal tariffs, plus two or three times to eight or nine times to even ten times the original tax. This increase in customs duties is truly alarming.

Japanese Silk Benefits from Tax

As a result, Chinese goods have to disappear from Vietnam because of the huge transportation costs and high tariffs. At the same time, Japanese goods replace Chinese goods. According to a new treaty established between Japan and France in May of this year, the goods that Chinese goods previously enjoyed the most-favored-nation treatment in Vietnam are now also enjoyed by Japan. As a result, Japanese goods are everywhere in the market. Overseas Chinese are heartbroken, but they can't do anything because they are in a foreign country.

Urgent Need to Seek Remedies

In recent years, the motherland has suffered from internal wars and the devastation of the communists, as well as the oppression and abuse of imperialist powers and strong neighbors. The national economy is already in a state of bankruptcy, commerce is stagnant, and society is restless. To seek remedies, the key figures in the central government must eliminate selfish opinions and unite to face foreign countries. In addition to seeking a peaceful and prosperous life for fellow countrymen at home, overseas Chinese should also be taken care of. The products of the industrial sector must be refined and improved. In foreign trade, we must pay attention to international commercial integrity and must not be careless, transporting inferior goods to foreign countries and losing credibility abroad. It is important to know that overseas Chinese urgently welcome the smooth sale of Chinese goods in foreign countries.

Silk Weaving Industry to Hold Discussions

The leaders of the silk weaving industry in this city, in view of the fact that the export sales of silk fabrics have plummeted due to the high tariffs imposed by various countries, have deeply worried about the national economy and the people's livelihood. In addition, the representative of the Chinese Chamber of Commerce in Cochinchina, Vietnam, returned to the country to petition, which made them feel that the matter was urgent. It is heard that discussions will be held soon to discuss solutions for relief.

Yang Jianping Resigns as Director of the Savings and Remittance Bureau

Yang Jianping, Director of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, telegraphed Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Communications yesterday, stating that he was submitting his resignation for review. I was appointed to this position in January of this year, and it has been nine months since then. With my humble talents, I have been mistakenly entrusted with important tasks. My rope is short and the well is deep, and I am in constant danger of failing. In addition, at the beginning of my appointment, I encountered the Shanghai Incident, which made it difficult to carry out the bureau's affairs. Furthermore, the postal panic in May had some impact on the savings and remittance business. I still racked my brains to try to develop it. Even during the market downturn, the amount of savings and remittances still increased. Now that the situation has stabilized and the market has gradually stabilized, the bureau's business urgently needs to be expanded. With my exhausted mind and energy, I am deeply afraid that I will not be able to cope with this important task. Rather than causing mistakes in the future, I would rather relinquish my responsibilities today. After thinking again and again, I can only submit my resignation to make way for the talented. All reasons for resignation are hereby submitted in writing for your approval. I respectfully request your approval and humbly ask you to appoint capable and virtuous individuals to take over as soon as possible. I am truly grateful.

Chinese Taxpayers' Association Begins Preparations for the 12th Election

The Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association has begun to investigate the qualifications of taxpayers within the boundary since the 1st of this month in order to conduct the 12th election. The association's announcement and letter to taxpayers are recorded below.

Announcement

The association holds an election every year. Now is the time for the 12th election. The taxpayer qualifications, such as address, of members may have changed. In addition to sending staff to investigate, correct, add and subtract based on the previous roster, there are bound to be omissions. Therefore, a public notice is hereby issued. Anyone who has resided within the Public Concession area for more than five years and (1) owns real estate with a land price of more than 500 taels, (2) pays more than 11 taels of property rent per year, or (3) pays more than 500 taels of rent per year and pays taxes, is requested to come to the association before December 15 to fill out the survey form, sign and seal it. If it is a representative of a group, company or store, the seal of the group, company or store must also be affixed in order to be included in the electoral roll. This matter concerns the right to vote. Please do not give it up. This announcement is hereby made for your information. Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association, November 3, 21st year of the Republic of China.

Separate Letters

Greetings, our association is organized by Chinese taxpayers in the concession. Representatives are re-elected once a year, and the representatives mutually elect 27 executive committee members to carry out the association's affairs and elect Chinese directors and Chinese committee members to participate in the work of the Municipal Council. Now is the time for the 12th election. The qualifications of members may have changed, so an investigation should be conducted. A staff member has been specially sent to deliver a copy of the qualification survey form and instructions for your review. Please fill in the items in the form in detail and affix your seal. Please submit it so that it can be included in the electoral roll. This matter concerns the right to vote of taxpayers. Please pay attention to it and do not give it up. This is what we hope for. With this, we wish you well.

Telegrams Concerning the Rice License Tax in Anhui

Wu Zhongxin replied to the Anhui groups: To the gentlemen of Anhui who are abroad, as reported by Shanghai newspapers, Zhongxin has governed Anhui for several months. All kinds of harsh and detailed taxes in the past, such as the special business tax, have been abolished one after another. Only the rice license tax has been designated by the central government as a special fund for road construction and is collected by a separate committee. In addition, the total budget of the province is more than 16 million yuan. After two rounds of reduction, it is now only more than 9 million yuan. The new budget will be implemented on November 1st of this year. I am afraid that the gentlemen are abroad and do not know all the details, or that the transmission is inaccurate. I hereby telegraph to inform you. Wu Zhongxin bows and sings.

The Anhui Association in Beijing opposed the rice license tax express mail telegram (titles omitted): Everyone, Recently, I read in the newspaper that the Anhui Provincial Government has suddenly restored the Food Administration Bureau of Chen Tiaoyuan's era, created a rice license tax in disguise of likin, and announced Li Yunqi, Lu Zhongnong, Yu Youquan, and others as members, and also directors of the rice license tax bureaus in Wuhu, Bengbu, Dashengguan, and other places. In addition, bureaus were established in Dashengguan, Xuanbu, Chenjiaqian, Wuyi, Tangyi, Jieshou, Jihua County, Wuhu, Bengbu, Anqing, Datong, Meihe, Huayang, Jiangba, Mingguang, Suxian, Linhuaiguan, and other places, and more than 30 people, including Yu Xianggu, Shu Tiexiang, Du Dongjiao, and Wang Lantian, were appointed as directors and inspectors. Such a large group of corrupt people is distributed throughout the north and south of Anhui Province. The harm they will cause is probably even worse than floods and fierce beasts. According to the published rules, a tax of 6 jiao is levied on each dan of rice exported by sailboat, 4 jiao by wheel transport, and 3 jiao on miscellaneous grains. The tax is several times higher than the previous likin. After years of natural disasters and banditry in Anhui, the people are almost all destitute, with starving corpses everywhere and wailing sounds filling the wilderness. The rural economy has indeed gone bankrupt. This year, except for the drought-stricken areas, there may be some rice and grain that can be exported, hoping to use it to regulate the social economy and seek the recovery of agriculture and commerce. However, the provincial authorities are bent on fulfilling their personal plans, colluding with shameless provincial officials, wantonly plundering, and without any scruples. They can absorb the blood and sweat of the common people, even if they wail and cry, they can turn a deaf ear. All of you are from Anhui. I don't know why you are so cruel. Moreover, when Chen Tiaoyuan established this tax last year, it was opposed by merchants throughout Anhui, and the Supervisory Yuan also filed an impeachment on the grounds that it conflicted with the central government's order to abolish likin. The Yuan and Ministry repeatedly ordered it to be abolished. How can we now violate the law and disobey public opinion, and revive this harsh policy that harms the people and the country in Anhui? As long as we have a breath left, we swear that we cannot recognize it. We hope that all our fellow Anhui compatriots will rise up together, resolutely resist, and demand that the provincial government abolish this chaotic order as soon as possible to relieve the people's suffering and maintain the law. If the provincial authorities are blinded by profit and cannot be persuaded, then our 30 million Anhui people must be of one mind, unite together, and support the rice merchants, resolutely refuse to pay this illegal tax, and at the same time organize the people's strength, and take immediate action in their respective locations to stop the establishment of this illegal bureau. If there are corrupt officials who disregard integrity, violate the public opinion of the entire Anhui Province, and rely on their authority to forcibly collect taxes, they are abandoning themselves to the people of Anhui. Then our compatriots in each of these places should make the greatest determination and impose strict sanctions. The members of this association vow to use all their strength as a backing for our oppressed compatriots. On the verge of sending this telegram, I am filled with emotion and do not know what to say. Anhui Association in Beijing bows.

Zha Liangzhao Comes South to Clarify Right and Wrong

Came to Shanghai to File a Lawsuit for the Anhui North Relief Affairs

The Anhui Association previously filed a lawsuit against the relief personnel in the Shanghai First Special District Court, listing Zha Liangzhao, a member of the Flood Relief Association, as the fourth defendant. Two court sessions have now been held. When Zha was sued, he was in Beiping and was suffering from hemorrhoids. Upon hearing the news, he telegraphed lawyer Zhang Xingyan to appear in court on his behalf. Zha has now come to Shanghai on the night before last (the 4th) specifically for this case, and his hemorrhoids have not fully recovered. Yesterday morning, he first went to the office of the Flood Relief Association to arrange a date to meet with Chairman Song of the association to report everything, and plans to ask a lawyer to urge the court to resume the trial as soon as possible in order to clarify the right and wrong, so as not to affect the progress of the relief efforts. The following is a record of Zha's conversation and his telegrams with Xu Shiying.

Zha's Statement

The Anhui North relief dispute began in the spring with a small number of Anhui North gentry attacking Quan Shaowu, the special commissioner of the relief affairs, and culminated in the recent lawsuit filed by the Anhui Association in Shanghai, Xu Shiying, and others in the Shanghai First Special District Local Court. In the meantime, right and wrong have been reversed, confusing social perceptions. Therefore, the truth of the matter must be made clear to the world, so that people's hearts can be rectified and relief affairs can be maintained. Since serving on the National Government Flood Relief Committee for a year, I have been diligent and selfless, and I am confident that I have not been selfish or violated the law. This time I came south, first for the sake of the personal credit and reputation of the relief personnel, and also for the honor of the entire National Government Flood Relief Committee and the credibility of various relief organizations in society. Second, I want to uphold justice, pay attention to the truth of the matter, and the court's judgment. After the right and wrong have been proven, I will protect those who are right and straight, and sanction those who are wrong and crooked, so that those who faithfully serve the society can bravely take on responsibilities, and those who reverse right and wrong and deceive society can disappear. The actions of the Anhui Association in Shanghai this time disregard the truth, and do not ask about the authority and responsibilities of the Flood Relief Committee. I believe it is the work of a small number of people. However, it is difficult to speculate on their intentions. Is it being fooled and deceived, or is it deliberately fabricating facts to damage personal reputation and the future of relief efforts? This layer is currently being investigated. Now I personally hope that the court will make a ruling on the right and wrong as soon as possible, so that the society can understand the truth and uphold justice, he said.

Telegrams

(1) Zha telegraphed Xu Shiying: Xu Jingren, member of the National Government Flood Relief Committee in Qiupu, I have hemorrhoids and underwent surgery in Tianjin. I have just been discharged from the hospital and came to Beiping. I read in various newspapers that the Anhui Association in Shanghai, led by you, filed a lawsuit in the Shanghai First Court for Anhui North relief affairs. I am also one of the defendants. After reading it, I am half-believing and half-doubting. Moreover, the allegations in the lawsuit do not match the facts. However, the matter concerns national relief and personal reputation, and the truth should be thoroughly investigated. I think you are a veteran of the country and a major person in charge of the relief association, so you should not follow the rumors and catch shadows. I am not yet convenient to express myself lightly. However, I would like to ask you to telegraph your intentions for leading the lawsuit. Zha Liangzhao bows. (2) Zha telegraphed the National Government Flood Relief Committee: Chairman Song of the Shanghai National Government Flood Relief Committee, I have just learned that Xu Shiying and others have filed a lawsuit in the Shanghai First Court for the Anhui North relief dispute, and have implicated Liangzhao, seriously defaming our association. Please listen to me carefully. I am filled with emotion. I have served the society, cherished my reputation, and valued it more than my life. The details of my handling of the Anhui North relief affairs are on file. If there are illegal facts as alleged, I will certainly bind myself to confess my guilt and apologize to the people of the country. Moreover, the plaintiffs first disregarded the facts and arbitrarily framed them. Second, they did not ask about the authority and responsibilities of our association and weaved charges against individuals. The spread of this matter is quite confusing, but it is even more important to the association's employment and the future of relief efforts. The truth should be thoroughly investigated. Please advocate for a thorough investigation to clarify the right and wrong. Furthermore, I am suffering from hemorrhoids and underwent surgery. I will come south to take care of the matter and explain everything as soon as I recover. I will first telegraph to inform you. Zha Liangzhao bows. (3) Xu Shiying replied to Zha's telegram: Brother Zha Mianzhong, I have respectfully received your telegram. The Anhui relief lawsuit took place in August. At that time, I was on leave to visit my father's illness in my hometown and did not hear about it. I returned to Shanghai on September 9th and learned that the association had followed the usual practice of listing the standing committee member's name as the first. I immediately stated my reasons to the association and asked lawyer Li Shirui to withdraw the case from the court on the 10th. I have recently received a telegram from Shanghai stating that the association has also published a correction in the newspaper. I am one of the members of the National Government Relief Committee and should be responsible for both merits and demerits. How can I file a lawsuit in my personal capacity? My duties and personality are at stake, and I will never do this. I specially reply to offer my condolences and gratitude. Your brother, Ying, bows. (4) Zha telegraphed Xu Shiying again: Xu Jingren, Qiupu, I have received your telegram. The Anhui relief lawsuit has reversed right and wrong, confused public opinion, and damaged personal reputation greatly. It has had even more impact on the future of relief efforts. You are from Anhui and are in charge of national relief efforts. You have a thorough understanding of the truth. Rather than showing that you are sharing the merits and demerits, you should rather uphold justice to rectify people's hearts and maintain your reputation. I hope you will make a wise decision. Zha Liangzhao bows.

Change of Location for the Two Railway Passenger Stations

Land Acquisition Reduced by Over 700 Mu

The new location for the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railway passenger terminal was surveyed by the Ministry of Railways near Zhenru. After the Ministry of Interior Affairs announced the land requisition, the residents within the designated area repeatedly petitioned for a reduction in the acquisition area due to its excessive size. The Ministry of Railways, in an effort to improve the layout and after further consideration, ultimately decided to slightly modify the original plan. All land south of the railway, originally intended for acquisition, was reduced by 198 meters from the railway side, resulting in a reduction of approximately 1,400 mu of land. Additionally, a piece of land west of Zhongshan Road and north of Jiaotong Road, approximately 700 mu in area, was purchased for the construction of various train depots and transfer tracks. This resulted in a net reduction of approximately 700 mu compared to the previously designated area. A request has been submitted to the Ministry of Interior Affairs for a re-announcement, ordering the administrations of the two railways to comply with the drawn boundaries within the acquisition area and to erect boundary markers for identification. A letter has also been sent to the Shanghai Municipal Government to announce the acquisition and to assist the Land Department of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways Construction Committee in handling all acquisition procedures.

Municipal Agricultural Experiment Field Displays Achievements During Chrysanthemum Exhibition

The Shanghai Municipal Agricultural Experiment Field, established just three years ago, has been actively conducting rice and wheat experiments. Taking advantage of the Chrysanthemum Exhibition, the field will display three years' worth of experimental results in a room at the Municipal Garden Field, providing visitors with an opportunity to observe and provide guidance. The displayed items are divided into the following categories: 1) Various varieties of cotton, rice, wheat, and beans; 2) Production comparisons; 3) Prevention of diseases and pests; 4) Types of fertilizers and methods of application; 5) Experimental plans and examination results; 6) Various new agricultural implements; 7) Various plant specimens; 8) Various experimental instruments. In addition, the field has also printed a summary of its activities to distribute to guests.

Qi Rengxi Appeals Zhang Meili Case

Qi Rengxi, formerly of the Guanhai Evening News and a native of Fujian, had an affair with his wife's younger sister, Zhang Meili, and cohabitated. They have now had seven children. Last winter, they developed animosity towards each other. Qi filed a lawsuit in the Second Special Court's Civil Division to end the relationship with Zhang. At the same time, Zhang filed a criminal self-accusation against Qi for offenses against public morals, and the two counter-sued each other. When the criminal lawsuits ended after two trials, Meili was defeated. She then continued with the civil suit. Zhang also filed a civil counterclaim, requesting that Qi be ordered to pay 140,000 yuan for the living and educational expenses of the children. It was then judged that both parties were allowed to end the relationship, and Qi was ordered to pay 500 yuan per month for the children's living and educational expenses. All of this has been reported in previous issues. It is now known that Qi Rengxi has expressed dissatisfaction with the original ruling regarding the payment of expenses. He believes that the children can be taken back for rearing and does not want to pay the expenses. He has presented reasons and hired a lawyer to submit a petition to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, filing an appeal. The High Court, based on the petition, summoned both parties to the court the day before yesterday, where Judge Zhao Zhenhai opened the third civil court for trial. First, the appellant, Qi Rengxi, stated his reasons for dissatisfaction and requested that the original judgment be revoked and a new judgment be issued. The respondent, Zhang Meili, stated that if the appellant can abide by the original judgment and pay the expenses on a monthly basis, then the children can move between the two parties in the future, etc. The court then instructed the two parties to go outside to reconcile and rescheduled the hearing.

Record of Gao Weicai Seducing and Abducting a Female Worker

Met on the Road and Forcibly Taken Home

Sentenced to Eight Months Imprisonment After Trial

Ding Xiuying, a woman from Yangzhou, is 28 years old, petite and exquisite. She has been working as a female worker in the fine yarn room of the Shenxin No. 7 Yarn Factory in Yangshupu. She lives at No. 35, Taopeng Road, Eight Li Lane. Her mother, Mrs. Chen, is 36 years old and widowed. She cherishes her daughter like a pearl. On the morning of November 25th, around 5:00 AM, Xiuying carried her work clothes and lunch basket to the factory for work. While passing through Pingliang Road, she met Gao Weicai, a fellow villager aged 20. He had known her for a long time and desired to marry her. When he met her on the road, he stepped forward, grabbed her hand, and snatched her work clothes and lunch basket. He used the excuse of going to Nanjing Road to play and dragged her onto the No. 8 tram. They transferred to a public bus at the Bund and went to Caojiadu Yidingpan Road. He pulled her to his home at No. 129 Ziyou Lane and locked her in the bedroom. He teased her in every possible way. At this point, Xiuying had no way to escape. It was as if she had entered a cage. No matter how she called for help, no one responded. She could only let him do as he pleased. She was raped, and her virtue was tarnished. The next day, she planned to return home, but she was not familiar with the road and had no money in her pocket. She was isolated and lost. Thinking of returning home, she was also afraid of her mother's blame. She was truly in a dilemma. After living there for five days, Gao's cousin, Huichang, secretly went to the home of Xiuying's mother, Ding Chen, and said, "Your daughter Xiuying has been taken care of. At least thirty yuan to go abroad can be used to find her." Mrs. Chen knew that this was what these people had done. She took the opportunity to go out and report to the Yulin Road Police Station, which sent Detective Ruan Taibin to arrest Gao Huichang and take him to the police station. After questioning, they learned the whereabouts of Miss Ding and rushed to Gao's house. They brought Xiuying out and she was taken back by her mother. Gao Huichang was sent to the First Special District Court to await sentencing. The day before yesterday afternoon, Hua Tan Ruan Taibin, who was handling this case, continued to apprehend Gao Weicai. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Bingrong presided over the interrogation at the Third Criminal Court. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, detailed the previous situation and stated that Gao Huichang, the defendant's brother, was only an accomplice and had nothing to do with the abduction, so he did not propose him as a witness. Then, Miss Ding Xiuying and her mother, Mrs. Chen, explained the previous situation. They questioned the defendant's confession that in May of this year, he lived at No. 44 Linqing Road, and the plaintiffs, mother and daughter, also lived there. He said that he and the plaintiffs, mother and daughter, also lived there, and that he was very familiar with them. Xiuying's grandmother allowed him to marry her, and he had asked friends to act as matchmakers. The rest of his confession was evasive, saying that he and Xiuying met on the No. 8 tram that morning, and she was willing to follow him home as his wife, etc. When Xiuying heard this, she was greatly displeased and scolded him. Judge Shen instructed the police lawyer, Zhang, to argue. He then sentenced Gao Zhaocai to six months imprisonment in court as a warning.

Wang Ao-xi Case Extended for Further Trial

The Police Department Has Not Yet Officially Prosecuted

Wang Ao-xi from Sichuan came to Shanghai last autumn and founded the "New Continent Daily." He often made provocative remarks, hoping to sow discord among various parties. The authorities sealed the newspaper and issued an arrest warrant. However, Wang remained oblivious and, together with Jiao Dao-song, a current member of the Military Affairs Commission, organized the "Power Society." Nanjing, considering their activities to be subversive, sent special agents to Shanghai to cooperate with detectives from the Public Concession Police to arrest Wang and Jiao at the China Hotel. Various manuscripts were seized from Wang, and they were handed over to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court for interrogation and detention pending further investigation. This has already been reported in this paper. This case was originally a request for assistance from the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau. The bureau had previously sent personnel to the Second Branch Court to request extradition, but the police lawyer stated that the "New Continent Daily" case occurred in the concession. Therefore, the police were still considering whether to prosecute Wang et al., and the extradition issue was temporarily shelved. Yesterday morning was the date for the continued trial. However, after considering the matter, the police still have not reached any conclusions as to whether or not to prosecute. A decision will be made after the verdict in the "New Continent Daily" case is announced. It is said that the verdict will be announced within days. Therefore, the police lawyer Li Zhi-shan specifically requested a one-week extension yesterday, while the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau still sent a legal advisor, lawyer Zhan Ji-feng, to the court to request extradition. Wang Ao-xi has retained lawyer Jiang Yi-ping to represent him in his defense. Judge Yu approved the police's request and ordered Wang et al. to be returned to custody. Therefore, whether this case will be extradited to the Public Security Bureau or handled by the Concession Court will not be known until the next hearing.

Case of Car Accident on Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway

Village Girl Injured in Collision

Driver Who Caused Accident Still Not Identified

Quan-zhen, the 13-year-old daughter of Gu Bing-gen, a resident of Fanwang Village, Seventh District, Fengxian County, Pudong, was walking past the Shagou Bridge on the afternoon of the 16th of last month when she was hit by a car with Public Concession license plate No. 11663 and Shanghai Municipal Government license plate No. 9150, which was speeding from Hangzhou to Shanghai. She suffered fatal injuries and died. The car did not stop after the accident but sped to Shanghai. The local villagers recorded the license plate number and reported it to the authorities, who sent personnel to investigate. It was found that the car belonged to the Fada Car Company on Xiafei Road in the French Concession. Yao Guangzhao, the local security chief, accompanied by witnesses, came to Shanghai and went directly to the Fada Car Company to identify the driver as Zhang Siwu. He reported this to the Fengxian County Government, which transferred the document to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau and reported it to the police department of the French Concession to send detectives to investigate. They found that there was no such person as Zhang Siwu at the Fada Car Company. The person they identified was Yan Miaojin. Yan was immediately taken to the police station and sent to the Second Criminal Court of the Second Special Court yesterday. After questioning by Judge Zhang Chao-zuo, the police lawyer first stated the case, followed by the family of the deceased complaining about the circumstances of the collision and requesting permission to transfer the defendant to the inland authorities for trial. Yan Miaojin confessed that he was indeed Yan Miaojin, not Zhang Siwu. He worked as a coppersmith at the Fada Car Company, not as a driver. Moreover, after checking the car company, there was no car that went to Hangzhou on the 16th of last month. He requested a clear investigation. Lin Rongliu, the manager of the Fada Car Company, also stated that the company did not have a car that was on a business trip on the 16th of last month and had records to prove it, requesting verification. Furthermore, the company did not have a person named Zhang Siwu. Yao Guangzhao, the local security chief of Fengxian County, also stated that after the accident, he accompanied witnesses to the defendant's car company to identify the defendant as the driver who caused the accident. At that time, when asked his name, he replied that his surname was Zhang and invited them to talk in the relief room. Later, Lu Xianglin, the dispatcher of the car company, sent people several times to mediate, but the matter was not settled. Zhou Bo-ang, the lawyer representing the plaintiff, stated that when the security chief and others went to the car company to inquire, the defendant admitted that his surname was Zhang, so Zhang Siwu was prosecuted. In short, there was witness testimony proving that the driver was indeed the defendant, who should be held responsible. The defendant was defended by lawyer Du Jimei, who stated that the plaintiff's claim was against Zhang Siwu, but the defendant was now Yan Miaojin, which was an error in the subject of the lawsuit. Moreover, the Fada Car Company's business trip records proved that there was no car that went to Hangzhou on that day. He requested that the case be dismissed. Judge Zhang announced the end of the debate and ruled that the defendant in this case was not Zhang Siwu and could not be extradited. The lawyer representing the plaintiff rose and stated that his client requested to file an appeal. The judge granted the request and ordered Yan to be released on bail.

Theater Performance at Minhang Orphanage Causes Disaster

Collapse of Stage Kills and Injures People

The Minhang Guangci Hospital, which is also an orphanage, hired the entire crew of the Shanghai Tianchan Stage to perform a theatrical performance at the hospital on the afternoon of the day before yesterday to raise funds. A very high stage was built. Ten thousand people came to watch the performance. The performance lasted until 11:00 PM when the stage collapsed due to the large crowd and the lack of sturdy construction. The audience all fell, and people were crushed by people, and were oppressed by wooden boards, etc. More than ten people were injured on the spot, and all were seriously injured. Among them, water policeman Li Xiaolong was crushed on the head and died immediately. The remaining seriously injured were sent to Shanghai Qu Zhiyou Hospital. Yesterday, the County Public Security Bureau reported to the local court, which immediately sent prosecutors to the scene to examine Li Xiaolong's injury to the back of the head and determined that he died as a result of his injuries. They ordered his family to collect the body. It is heard that three more of the injured died yesterday, but the deaths have not been reported to the hospital for verification.

News from Various Native-Place Associations

The Huizhou Native-Place Association in Shanghai sent a fast mail telegram stating: The Huizhou-Yang Chamber of Commerce in Hong Kong forwarded to various legal entities and the entire citizenry of Huiyang: Upon reading the Yangri telegram, we were shocked to learn that the County Magistrate of Huiyang, in the name of raising government funds, was in fact scheming to collect money by force. Hearing this from afar, we share the same indignation. Huiyang County has suffered repeated wars and countless disasters. There are scars everywhere, and refugees are on the roads. The people are starving, and there are corpses in the fields. As a County Magistrate, one should care about the people's suffering, pacify and gather the laborers, implement conservation policies, and cultivate local vitality. However, he abandons this and puts the cart before the horse, establishing nominal functions and planning to collect a field tax from the county's money and grain items, amounting to as much as three yuan per mu, stripping the last thread from the poor and poisoning the entire county. If the County Council had not opposed it earlier and the Chamber of Commerce in Hong Kong had not appealed later, how could the descendants of Huiyang have survived? Collecting field tax is a harmful and oppressive policy, unheard of not only in this province but also rare in the entire country. If the County Magistrate recognizes the overall situation and governs the people, he should practice austerity on the existing government funds, recruit talented people to assist in the affairs, and increase administrative efficiency. If he truly benefits the people and achieves outstanding results, then the people will naturally be willing to contribute. How can he have such a thought of draining the pond to catch all the fish after a situation filled with holes. It is heartbreaking! The members of our association, living in Shanghai, are spiritually connected to Ehuling. We respect and fulfill our obligation and respond to the call. We hope that the gentlemen of the County Council will strictly supervise, and that fellow villagers at home and abroad will rise up to resist, prevent corruption, and benefit our hometown. The telegram is full of sincerity, and we cannot express our utmost wishes. Shanghai Huizhou Native-Place Association bowed to the East,

Record of the Diamond Sutra Dharma Assembly

Old Lay Buddhist Jiang Wei-nong of the Shengxin Lianshe at No. 712 Ci Hui Li, the intersection of Seymour Road and Weihaiwei Road, gives lectures on the Diamond Sutra every Tuesday and Friday evening at 7:30 PM. He has been lecturing several times. People come from all directions to listen, and it is quite popular. Jiang Gong is versed in all kinds of learning, and is familiar with hundreds of schools of thought, but returns to the inner classics. He has extensively studied various sects and integrated his mind with Prajna. In this lecture, he can capture the strengths of various theories, integrate them, and use clear words and allegories to open up the meaning of the scriptures. He often says that Prajna clarifies the true emptiness, so as to break the world's greed and attachment, which is truly a good medicine for saving the times. It is no less than a dose of Qingliang powder. But the true emptiness is inseparable from the wonderful existence, and it is by no means a pessimistic withdrawal from the world. And when the truth is clear, the direction is correct. From the body to the use, the cure can be expected. Westerners often come to our country to lecture on Buddhism. How can we not seek to enlighten ourselves? Moreover, the first thing in Buddhism is to understand the truth. If one can understand the principle, then it is easier for those who recite the Buddha to gain strength. Then Prajna Pure Land is really not two things. The audience thinks that Jiang Gong's appearance is stern, his words are eloquent, like counting treasures, deeply manifested, and they are all happy and admiring. And his atmosphere is full, and his learning is deep. Every time he is seen laughing and relaxed after leaving the lecture, he is truly one who can empty his heart and has a deep inner compassion.

Correspondence

To the esteemed editor-in-chief of the Shen Bao:

Regarding the article published in the Shen Bao on October 27th concerning the invention of "Maddi Tea" by the Zideng Research Institute, which stated that "drinking tea damages the brain and harms the stomach, causing hair loss and wrinkles," these are all unfounded claims. It should be known that our country's foreign trade relies heavily on silk and tea as major export products, which are vital to the national economy and the people's livelihood. Throughout history, neither Chinese nor foreign scholars have ever argued that Chinese tea is harmful to the human body. The Zideng Research Institute, however, dares to make such arbitrary pronouncements in the newspapers, causing outrage among thousands of tea industry colleagues in Shanghai. Many members of our association originally intended to negotiate directly with the institute, but were persuaded to disperse by our chairman, Wang Yinting, after repeated劝导. We believe that while the institute's invention is welcome news for the nation, it should not boast about itself by attacking others. Therefore, our association has submitted a report to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting an investigation and correction to prevent further propaganda detrimental to domestic products. Otherwise, the institute should be held responsible for any disputes that may arise. We request that this letter be published in the "Correspondence" column to appease public anger. We are deeply grateful.

Respectfully,

Shanghai Tea Trade Association

November 5th

To the esteemed editor-in-chief:

I aspire to dedicate myself to the cause of national salvation. However, I was distressed to read a correction notice in the "Correspondence" column of both the Shen Bao and Xin Shen Bao a few days ago (the 2nd) bearing my name, Zhang Jie. It is regrettable that I am a native of Shangyu, Zhejiang, and my name since childhood has been Zhang Jie, and I have never changed it since entering society. This Mr. Zhang Jie is indeed a case of the same name. This is detrimental to my future prospects and related to my association duties, therefore I implore you to grant me a correction and wish the chief writer of Shen Bao good health.

Respectfully,

Zhang Jie

November 4th, Special Delivery

Judge Feetham's Report on the Shanghai International Settlement, Volume 4 (14)

11. Concerning the remuneration of auditors, it should be determined by the Board of Directors, so that when the two taxpayers' meetings each elect an auditor, the remuneration of the two auditors can be uniform. The Board of Directors should decide and announce the amount of remuneration before holding the election.

B. Security of Tenure

12. Whether auditors should be elected annually or every few years is a question. Auditors should not be changed frequently. Setting a term of several years would help ensure their independence when performing their duties. Therefore, I suggest that the term of auditors should not be less than three years, and it should be stipulated that the annual remuneration during the term should not be different (Note 6).

C. Powers of the Auditors

13. To enable auditors to faithfully perform their duties, they must have the right to obtain all relevant information. The city's regulations sometimes stipulate that if there are violations of the law, expenditures made without prior approval from the Municipal Council, or losses due to negligence or improper actions, the auditors may order the relevant council members or officials to compensate for the losses and may sue the respective members to recover the funds. If such powers are exercised, auditors should also have the power to summon witnesses, administer oaths, and interrogate them in accordance with customary practice. (To be continued)

Free Talk

Quotations from the Nonagenarian Ma Xiangbo

Shops, Private Schools, Families, and Handicrafts

— Jing Ji

The old man Xiang recalled... In the past, shops served as private schools, and women in families practiced handicrafts. When the sun set, there were fewer pedestrians on the road and fewer customers at the door, so the shop would close. Every shop offered a supplementary private school. The accountant was the teacher, and the young apprentices were the students. The curriculum involved learning abacus calculations and calligraphy. This was generally the case! Because the accountant was the voluntary teacher of the young apprentices, his position became even more respected when the apprentices became shop assistants! Good shop assistants, knowing gratitude, would naturally not forget the essential commercial knowledge they received from the accountant, thus maintaining considerable respect for their teacher. In this way, wouldn't a shop be harmonious, stable, and able to develop? I wonder what the current customs are like?

I remember in 1904, when I went to Japan, I saw their enthusiasm for supplementary learning. In ordinary schools, during physics and geometry classes, many older people, perhaps the students' fathers or elder brothers, stood in the corridors outside the classroom, listening intently to the teachers who were lecturing and gesturing. This eagerness to learn left a lasting impression on me!

Speaking of families, women used to learn handicrafts. Someone told me that a woman's robe now costs several dollars in labor to have made at a tailor shop! When I heard this, I thought it was right! Why can't they make it themselves? They deserve to complain about the high cost! In the past, the older generation in families, grandmothers who lived to be seventy or eighty years old, still supervised the women in the household to do needlework. Even if the family was well-off, they would still make cotton-padded clothes to give to the poor! Now, the customs are different!

Naturally, the old man Xiang felt a lot of emotion when talking about this!

Old and New

— Bi

| Old Brand, New Product |

In this day and age, everything must be new. For example, when it comes to clothing, long robes and jackets are no longer fashionable. Modern friends must wear a Western suit. Just wearing a suit is enough to show that you're modern, but when it comes to the style of the suit, it must be a 1933 model to show that you're modern to the future. Taking one example as a hundred, drawing inferences from one case, if you're not buying anything, then that's it, but if you're buying, you must choose the newest style, otherwise you'll be outdated and not considered a person of the times.

But the situation is often fiercely contradictory. The more you want to buy the newest, most recently manufactured items, the more you insist on going to old stores. For example, if there are two stores selling the same items from the same source, one founded in the first year of the Tongzhi reign (1862) and the other opened in the twenty-first year of the Republic (1932), the store founded in the Tongzhi era will definitely have better business than the one opened in 1932. In the end, it all comes down to the Tongzhi-era store benefiting from the reputation of its brand.

The old Lu Gaojian restaurant in Suzhou and the old Zhengxing Restaurant in the restaurant district are such well-known old brands. The old family physicians who have been Confucian doctors for seven or eight generations, and the old hospitals founded in the Tongzhi era, are often overwhelmed with patients. Whether it's food or goods, if the store's staff says, "This is the oldest of old brands," it will definitely be welcomed. But if a "newest product" is added under the "oldest of old brands," it will definitely be even more popular. Because in this era, only the brand is good for being old. When it comes to goods, the newer, the better.

Our newspaper can be considered the oldest brand in the newspaper industry. No matter what newspaper people in the interior read, they all call it the Shen Bao. From this, one can see the seniority of our newspaper. But the value of being old lies in the brand. The content is selling a "new" product. Although our newspaper is as old as it gets, the content is cutting-edge new. Even this "Free Talk" column, though it's an old brand, its content changes daily.

A Scene from the Capital War

— Tianfang

Piles of red packages, green packages, big ones, small ones, sugared chestnuts displayed all over the streets. Gramophones, gongs and drums, the smell of charcoal, deafening calls for sales... As you walk through every alley, you can see a scene from the time-sensitive commercial capital war. Indeed, in this era of great change, everything has lost its constancy. You see "huge discount" advertisements pasted as thickly as bedbugs in summer, so many that they're annoying. The sounds of Western medicine fill the streets, blowing wildly like they've gone mad. People's faces are silent, money is as stagnant as blood, and society is like a sick ox, heading towards decline. Everyone is just waiting, waiting for new life to be born from the collapse.

The Success of a Deformed Love

— Ke Dingcang

It's Not a Strange Story

I had already heard my cousin Li Shucheng say that there was a classmate at their school (Hangzhou) who displayed very feminine behavior in his speech and actions, but he always refused to admit that he was a woman.

In Hangzhou, girls are referred to as "Big Green Ladies," so the classmates at XX School gave him this nickname. Whenever he heard this name, he would often twist his neck and pout, showing an ambiguous expression. Doesn't this prove that the classmates' imitation was correct?

Shucheng also said that he shared a room with four classmates who were about the same age. Coincidentally, the one who got along best with him was his fellow villager from Shaoxing. So they were closer to each other, and the two of them would still be talking and laughing with great interest late into the night, after the other two had fallen asleep. One time, one of the other two, seeing them like this every night, pretended to be asleep and secretly observed them. By chance, that very night, he uncovered their secret and clearly learned that he was a physically deformed person. The next day, the news spread by that person like wildfire throughout the school, though no one said anything about it to their faces.

Later, the winter break started, and when school reopened this spring, neither of them came back.

XX XX XX

Recently, Shucheng sent me a letter saying, "The deformed person and his partner that I told you about before actually got married this early summer. Some classmates at school received a photo of the two of them with their offspring a month ago. He looks even more charming, and the offspring is male, looking almost exactly like him. From this, it seems that physically deformed people also have the possibility of marriage."

Brother Qiu's New Scam

— Bi Jun

| One of Shanghai's Dark Secrets |

The beautiful Shanghai is full of variety, and nothing is too strange to find. Even scams involve cunning schemes and are constantly evolving. Some people even make this their profession, seizing money, hiding in hotels, indulging in prostitution, and spending lavishly.

Recently, there is a person named Qiu, around twenty-three or four years old, with a dark complexion, a thin body, gold teeth, and wearing the title of leader of the Nanyang Chinese Overseas Asian Walking Group, dressed in Boy Scout uniform or hunting clothes, carrying a donation book and soliciting donations from various companies, stores, foreign firms, and organizations. He claims to have just returned from Yunnan, with a list of local people as proof, and plans to go to Tibet, Qinghai, and India, and has printed stationery for a film crew to explore and take photos everywhere. Listeners often admire his youthful ambition and adventurous walking, so many are generous in donating. This scammer can speak simple English, so Europeans and Americans are also sometimes fooled. After receiving a donation, he asks someone to sign the book as proof. If he meets a domestic goods factory or a business shop that is preparing to sell products to Nanyang landlords but has no way to do so, he uses his eloquent tongue, saying that he can introduce them, and first takes samples as a promotion, etc. Products such as Wudi brand cosmetics, Yixin brand toothbrushes, Chen Jiageng's products, and Shi Dezhi's products are all taken away in large quantities. Once he gets them, he immediately sells them, exchanges them for money, and wanders in major hotels, seeking pleasure and spending his absurd life.

I have encountered several scams of this kind, all the same trick. When talking to relatives and friends, they also said the same thing. One night, I happened to be driving past the Shenzhou Hostel when I suddenly heard a rickshaw puller shouting in pain and arguing over the fare, with the sound of a passenger raising his hand to slap him. The momentum was fierce. Taking a closer look, the passenger was none other than Brother Qiu who was walking. I learned from the rickshaw puller that he had come from the Small Garden. Alas! Such a distance, afraid to trouble your jade feet, I wonder how he walks tens of thousands of miles? It is said that he often takes cars or motorboats, and goes to the Huangpu River with prostitutes to enjoy himself. He spends the whole day leisurely, never leaving the foreign concessions. As for the so-called list of people in Yunnan and other places, if you look closely at the handwriting, most of it is done by one person, and the seals are also mostly counterfeits.

Now, the Northeastern refugees are crying out for help, and the righteous army is fighting desperately against the Japanese. Financial assistance is urgently needed. How can we tolerate this thief swindling people? I sincerely hope that people in society will be vigilant and not make unnecessary sacrifices.

The Rotary Club is Lost in a Novel

Crossroads of Death (6)

— Fan Yanqiao

Soon, Aigu was assimilated by Siyin and guided by Han's young mistress, and she changed bit by bit: first, she changed her clumsy, large, and rough hair into a small, exquisite, and shiny style; second, she shortened the length of her upper garment by two-thirds, reduced her figure by one-fifth, and changed the material from blue cloth to white bamboo cloth. Even her socks and shoes were changed to look different from before, so she looked like an uncut jade that had been polished by a jade worker, suddenly shining brightly, proving that the old saying "clothes make the man" has meaning.

Han's young mistress said to the young master: "Muliang, look at my skills! Aigu has been here for less than a month and has already undergone a transformation."

Muliang said excitedly: "Aigu is born to be a promising talent. If it were any other vulgar girl, no matter how much you dressed her up, it would be useless."

Han's young mistress took out a bottle of snow powder from the drawer of the dressing table and said: "If you let her apply this stuff often, I guarantee she will be even more pleasing."

Muliang laughed and said: "Pleasing to whom?"

Han's young mistress pointed her index finger at Muliang's forehead and said: "Pleasing to you."

Muliang gave a few dry laughs. Han's young mistress casually pressed the electric bell hanging in the air. After a short time, Aigu came in. Muliang carefully looked at her from head to toe again, especially paying attention to her round face, and her full and subtly restrained chest, which was thought-provoking. He then turned his head to look at his wife and felt that his wife no longer had the beauty of a virgin, and he firmly believed that the golden age of a woman was only a period from full development to the eve of marriage. Seeing that Han's young mistress had given her the snow powder, she took it, smiled sweetly, and bashfully said a word, inadvertently pouring her eyes on Muliang. Muliang's eyes had not moved for a long time, and they met. Aigu could no longer calm down, turned around and left, lowered her head, probably her cheeks were flushed with red clouds. Muliang said with emotion: "If she is further enlightened by you and bathed in the fragrance of Paris, I am afraid she will be a 'queen of maids'."

Han's young mistress was naturally very proud when she heard this, and after a while, she said in a low voice: "I'm afraid you'll be enchanted."

Muliang still gave a few dry laughs. After a long time without speaking, he turned on the gramophone and listened to a few records of folk tunes, and this evening passed.

Although the exchange rate was quoted half a cent higher, the domestic market was not loose, and the bank's appetite was still strong. Therefore, the various firms hedged and sold US dollars, and then recovered the strips. It was also rumored that the Central Bank continued to purchase spot goods, so the market price rose from low to high. Not long after, Tongtai, Changfu, Taiheng, Yifeng, Yongyuan, Maoyong, etc. sold out, falling to 4 taels and 6 qian. Soon after, Dadecheng worked hard to drag in, and Daxingyong, Hengyu, Dafengyong and Hedging also competed to buy. It was also rumored that the Central Bank traded 420 bars of spot goods with US dollars, so the price was raised by two taels. After 11 o'clock, it was 46 taels and a half. In an instant, Yifeng, Hengxing, etc. went to the market and sold 5 or 6 hundred bars, losing one tael immediately. Soon after, it added 4 or 5 qian, because the entrants were not silent, but Zhifengyong Hengyu also sold, and Hengxing sold continuously, so at 11:50, it was 4 taels and 7 qian. However, the Bank of America in December continued to absorb a total of 875, which should be pulled to 5 taels and 6 qian. By noon, it was 44 taels and 9 qian, and it continued to rise to 46 taels, so the goods were raised by 6 qian, a drop of 1.9 taels compared to the day before (according to the posted price). According to half a day, the maximum was 6 taels and a half, the minimum was 2 taels, and the fluctuation was 4 taels and a half. The bare bars added 11 taels.

Securities and Bond Market Increasingly Desolate

|Price Slightly Declining, Trend Increasingly Stagnant|

Yesterday (the 5th), the situation in various bond markets at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange showed that several markets were still opening. Total transactions amounted to 22,300 yuan, including over 6,000 yuan each for the Reorganization Bonds of 19 and the Salt Tax bonds. Other transactions were minimal. The futures market was even more desolate, with sluggish trading throughout the day and sparse activity between various boards. Many monthly futures contracts did not open fully. It is estimated that total transactions in the morning and afternoon markets were only about 900,000 yuan, totaling 1,790,000 yuan. This included 300,000 to 400,000 yuan each for the Unified Salt Tax bonds and Reorganization Bonds, 170,000 to 180,000 yuan for the Customs Bonds of 20, and only several tens of thousands of yuan for others. The market sentiment was one of cautious observation, and the bond market atmosphere was extremely dull. Large investors remained inactive, and even small investors were less active than before. As a result, the trend became increasingly stagnant, with morning and afternoon markets still hovering around 10 to 20 cents, a slight decline compared to the previous day, amounting to about 20 cents. The market situation has returned to a state of quiescence.

The cotton market suddenly rallied, as profit-takers took the opportunity to cover their short positions after a sharp drop. At the same time, American cotton also trended upward, further tightening market conditions. However, major sellers remained unusually calm and maintained their intention to sell on any rallies. The future of the cotton market still depends on the movements of American cotton.

Private Estimates of American Cotton All Increased

A New York telegram on the 4th reported that the Foxdick Bureau's estimate for the current season's new cotton production is 11,175,000 bales, an increase of 336,000 bales compared to the previous estimate (October 5th). The amount of cotton ginned is 8,700,000 bales. The average estimate from brokers on the New York Cotton Exchange is 11,410,000 bales, an increase of 425,000 bales compared to the previous estimate.

Hedging Sales of American Cotton Decreased Last Week

A New York telegram on the 4th reported on the cotton market situation for the week, stating that the industry demand in the raw cotton market this week, including domestic and foreign countries such as Japan, seemed sufficient to absorb all daily hedging sales. However, buying interest was limited to lower prices, and market prices were slightly lower. Political instability restricted general trade, and there was a clear trend of waiting to see how things would develop. There were some arbitrage activities between New York and Liverpool due to changes in the British pound exchange rate. Liverpool may have bought in slightly in anticipation of greater optimism in Manchester and hopes for an early resolution to the Lancashire cotton industry labor dispute. The average of the initial four private reports on cotton-producing areas at the end of October was 11,539,000 bales, compared to the average estimate of 11,279,000 bales at the same time last month. Spot cotton basis prices were stable, and there were relatively few sales in the interior.

Dramatic Fluctuations in the Grain and Flour Market

Yesterday, after the close of the flour market in the morning, there were significant changes in the prices of various months. At the initial opening, the price of foreign wheat rebounded by about 30-40 cents, and a certain factory also raised its price accordingly. Therefore, after the opening of the auction, the price rebounded by 2-3 cents compared to the previous day. However, after the second board, both Fufu and Fulong factories dumped their products, and the offering of Australian wheat continued unabated. Transactions could be made at any time from 3.55 taels to 3.5 taels. The market atmosphere was like a boat without a rudder, subject to blows. After that, the price fell sharply step by step, falling by 2-4 cents compared to the opening price. When the afternoon market opened, the situation was even worse than in the morning. Because most of the bulls could no longer hold on due to fundamental reasons, they all cut their losses. The severity of the situation was the first time since the establishment of the exchange. For example, December fell to a low of 1.685 taels, January to 1.66 taels, February to 1.665 taels, March to 1.68 taels, and April to 1.69 taels, all new record lows. It was then rumored that major players in the cotton yarn industry were buying in, intending to raise prices, and there was a gradual rebound. After the fourth board, transactions became clearer, and the situation stabilized. As for the oversupply of global agricultural products, if producers forcibly raise spot prices and prevent widespread circulation, they will almost isolate themselves. As a result, the current month was better by 1.75 cents compared to the previous day, December was slightly better by 5 cents, January by 2.5 cents, February by 5 cents, and March and April by 7.5 cents.

Wheat Prices: Futures Down, Spot Flat

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning and afternoon, there were signs of weakness in the prices of various months. Although the price of foreign wheat was better by 20-40 cents, the external environment remained unfavorable. Furthermore, in the near future, the oversupply of foreign countries will shift to China. This situation will inevitably play out under the unrestricted flow of foreign wheat. Therefore, people were panicked. Although transactions were not smooth, the market unanimously declined. If foreign wheat continues to be priced low, the market is likely to weaken further. As a result, the current month and December each fell by 3 cents, January and February fell by 5 cents, March fell by 4 cents, and April remained unchanged. The spot wheat market slightly improved, and the opening price turned flat. The opening prices were 3.25 taels for Gaoyou wheat, 3.32 taels for Yaowan wheat, and 3.26 taels for Saiying wheat, with a total of over 400 dan.

Popularity of Hand-Picked Chunmee Green Tea Sales Continues in France

British firms such as Jinlong and Tianxiang were searching and buying with all their might due to demand from Morocco. The market prices were also slightly firmer than before. Coal: Fuzhou Coal Dust Subject to Additional Tax

Since the puppet state occupied the Northeast Customs, all goods coming from the Northeast must pay import duties. Since Fuzhou coal dust is produced in Fengtian, the Ministry of Finance has ordered the Customs to also levy taxes according to regulations. Yesterday, a certain company in this port shipped 1,500 tons of new goods, which have already been taxed. However, the cost has increased as a result. Yesterday, when the market opened, the price was raised by 5 cents per ton.

The Sugar Market's Coarse Granulated White Sugar Sees Stagnant Prices

Yesterday, the sugar market saw a very weak trend due to the repeated decline in bidding prices. The quoted price for No. 24 coarse granulated white sugar remained at 14.9 taels, and the price for machine-ground fine granulated white sugar was also 14.9 taels, but there were no transactions, resulting in a stagnant situation. The prices for No. 20 and No. 18 medium granulated white sugar and No. 8, 9, and 10 Dutch red sugar also remained unchanged. Yesterday, 130 bags of locally produced Grade 2 white sugar, which were transported by the Taikoo Company's Jinan ship, were fully released by the Jianbang firm at a price of 13.8 taels. It is said that the buyer's desired price is above 14 taels, but it is difficult to achieve because of the competition from the local factory's products in Shanghai.

North-South Goods: Longkou Vermicelli Market Prices Are Inverted

|Sluggish Sales in Shanghai|

Recently, the sales of Longkou vermicelli have been sluggish, and the market prices have fallen by 2-3 cents. There have been no deliveries of goods. The previous price was less than 19 taels, and now various dealers are reluctant to buy. Therefore, there have been no transactions between the dealers and customers. It is especially difficult to make a profit because the local price is higher than the price in Shanghai. The future market must wait for the sales to become active before there is any hope of improvement. Yesterday, the top brand Long vermicelli was sold at 19 taels, and Yantai vermicelli at 16.5 taels. The market situation is weak.

Oil Market: White Tung Oil Market at the Time of Old and New Transition

The new white tung oil season has arrived, but foreign firms are still showing a cautious approach. There are rumors about the arrival of Xianggu tung oil in Wuhan, causing the Wuhan market to linger in a state of fluctuation. It can be said with certainty that the market cannot develop and can only maintain the current situation. However, the factories in various producing areas in Zhejiang are urgently engaged in the work of starting to manufacture new goods, and the market is filled with an atmosphere of hoping for lower prices. According to investigations, the purchase price of tung seeds in various producing areas means that the cost of Shanghai combined is slightly above 22 taels per dan. Therefore, a Hangzhou dealer opened sales in Shanghai a few days ago, selling 600-700 dan of futures oil for December delivery at prices between 23.46 yuan, while the spot price was 24.24 yuan. According to reports from those familiar with the conditions in the producing areas, the price of the futures sales was already low. If the price falls further, the cost concerns in the producing areas may prevent it. Local firms in this port, because they are aware that the sales market is not very active, are not being too greedy. However, they seem to be slightly cheaper than Wuhan tung oil. Therefore, future purchases should focus on Zhejiang tung oil.

Metals: Over 3,000 Dan Opened Yesterday

Yesterday, the metal market situation saw both activity and quietness. There were significant transactions in English steel plates, new foreign silver dollars, tinplate, and new lead wire. It is said that the total number of transactions reached over 3,000 dan, causing the prices in various markets to rise sharply. English steel plates were priced at 8.25 taels per dan for 0.02-inch thickness, 6 taels for 0.05-inch thickness, and 5.75 taels for 0.075-inch thickness, all rising step by step compared to the previous market prices. Those who were slower to procure were all sighing with regret. It was found that the most active buyers were from Qingdao, Tianjin, and the Yangtze River areas. Apart from these, others did not inquire. As for other varieties, such as copper, tin, bronze, angle iron, railway skin, and new iron wire, they were all stagnant and motionless. Therefore, the future of the market is inevitably bleak.

Ribbed Steel Bars Increase in Price by One Tael

Recently, the price of ribbed steel bars has increased due to the limited supply in the market and a sharp increase in exports. It is estimated that the price for all varieties is 67 taels per ton, an increase of one tael compared to the previous price. There is also a growing short interest in the market, so the future price trend is expected to rise further.
